<p>The <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NHL_season" title="2010–11 NHL season">2010–11 season</a> began on October 9, 2010, with a pre-game ceremony to commemorate the team's 40-year anniversary. <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Sedin" title="Henrik Sedin">Henrik Sedin</a> was officially named in the ceremony as the team's new captain, replacing Roberto Luongo, who had relinquished his captaincy in the off-season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CaptainHenrik_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-CaptainHenrik-107">[106]</a></sup> The Canucks played the Los Angeles Kings, their first opponent in their inaugural season in 1970; both teams wore their original uniforms used in the Canucks' inaugural game. Throughout the season, the Canucks continued to celebrate their 40th anniversary with the creation of the "Ring of Honour", a permanent in-arena display commemorating their most significant players from past years. Four players were inducted during the campaign – Orland Kurtenbach, Kirk McLean, Thomas Gradin and Harold Snepsts. In December 2010, the Canucks also honoured Markus Naslund by retiring his number 19 jersey. Naslund had retired two years after leaving the Canucks in 2008.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Henrik_Sedin_Campbell_Bowl.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2000" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Henrik_Sedin_Campbell_Bowl.jpg/300px-Henrik_Sedin_Campbell_Bowl.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Henrik_Sedin_Campbell_Bowl.jpg/450px-Henrik_Sedin_Campbell_Bowl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Henrik_Sedin_Campbell_Bowl.jpg/600px-Henrik_Sedin_Campbell_Bowl.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Henrik_Sedin_Campbell_Bowl.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Henrik Sedin accepts the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Campbell_Bowl" title="Campbell Bowl">Campbell Bowl</a> on behalf of the Canucks as the 2011 Western Conference champions.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the second half of the campaign, the Canucks pulled ahead in their battles for the Western Conference and Presidents' Trophy titles with the Detroit Red Wings and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Flyers" title="Philadelphia Flyers">Philadelphia Flyers</a>, respectively, widening the gap as the season closed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010-11-Battle_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010-11-Battle-109">[108]</a></sup> On March 29, 2011, the Canucks clinched first place in the West for the first time in team history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> Two days later, they accomplished another first by securing the Presidents' Trophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> Finishing with 54 wins and 117 points, the 2010–11 team broke the previous Canuck records in both categories by significant margins. Individually, numerous Canucks players had career years. Daniel Sedin won the Art Ross Trophy with a league-leading 104 points, marking the first time in NHL history that two brothers won the award in back-to-back years. Meanwhile, Ryan Kesler tied Daniel Sedin for the team goal-scoring lead, with 41 goals. In goal, Roberto Luongo and rookie backup <a href="/wiki/Cory_Schneider" title="Cory Schneider">Cory Schneider</a> captured the <a href="/wiki/William_M._Jennings_Trophy" title="William M. Jennings Trophy">William M. Jennings Trophy</a> for recording the lowest team <a href="/wiki/Goals_against_average" title="Goals against average">goals against average</a> (GAA) in the NHL.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_Stanley_Cup_run">2011 Stanley Cup run</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2011 Stanley Cup run">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Entering the <a href="/wiki/2011_Stanley_Cup_playoffs" title="2011 Stanley Cup playoffs">2011 Stanley Cup playoffs</a>, the Canucks were paired with the eighth-seeded and defending Stanley Cup champion Chicago Blackhawks, who had eliminated Vancouver in the previous two years. While Vancouver initially took a 3–0 lead in the series, Chicago came back to also win three straight games and force the series into a Game 7. Luongo, who had a history of struggling against the Blackhawks, was pulled in Games 4 and 5; he also began Game 6 on the bench in favour of Cory Schneider before returning as the starter in Game 7. In the deciding game, Vancouver held a 1–0 lead with less than two minutes remaining in regulation when they gave up a shorthanded goal to Chicago captain <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Toews" title="Jonathan Toews">Jonathan Toews</a>. Forced into overtime, winger <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Burrows" title="Alexandre Burrows">Alexandre Burrows</a> scored his second goal of the game following a failed clearing attempt by Chicago defenceman <a href="/wiki/Chris_Campoli" title="Chris Campoli">Chris Campoli</a> to win the series.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ryan_Kesler_03-2010a.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1510" data-file-width="1133" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ryan_Kesler_03-2010a.jpg/220px-Ryan_Kesler_03-2010a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ryan_Kesler_03-2010a.jpg/330px-Ryan_Kesler_03-2010a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Ryan_Kesler_03-2010a.jpg/440px-Ryan_Kesler_03-2010a.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ryan_Kesler_03-2010a.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ryan_Kesler" title="Ryan Kesler">Ryan Kesler</a> spent the first 10 seasons of his <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a> career with the Canucks.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the Conference Semi-finals, the Canucks faced the defensive-minded <a href="/wiki/Nashville_Predators" title="Nashville Predators">Nashville Predators</a>, led by goaltender <a href="/wiki/Pekka_Rinne" title="Pekka Rinne">Pekka Rinne</a>. Of the 14 goals Vancouver scored in the low-scoring series, Canucks centre Ryan Kesler registered a point in 11 of them, helping the Canucks defeat the Predators in six games. Facing the <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Sharks" title="San Jose Sharks">San Jose Sharks</a> in the Conference Finals, captain Henrik Sedin led the Canucks with 12 points in the five-game series. Vancouver defeated San Jose four-games-to-one with a double-overtime winner from defenceman <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Bieksa" title="Kevin Bieksa">Kevin Bieksa</a> in the fifth game.</p>
<p>Advancing to the <a href="/wiki/2011_Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="2011 Stanley Cup Finals">Stanley Cup Finals</a> for the first time since 1994, the Canucks opened the fourth round against the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a> with a 1–0 win in Game 1. Winger <a href="/wiki/Raffi_Torres" title="Raffi Torres">Raffi Torres</a> scored the winning goal with 18.5 seconds remaining. The following game, the Canucks won 3–2 in overtime with Burrows scoring the winner 11 seconds into the extra frame, making it the second fastest overtime goal in Stanley Cup Finals history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> As the series shifted from Rogers Arena to <a href="/wiki/TD_Garden" title="TD Garden">TD Garden</a> for Games 3 and 4, Boston tied the series with 8–1 and 4–0 victories. Game 3 marked the highest score by one team in a Finals game since the Colorado Avalanche defeated the Florida Panthers in <a href="/wiki/1996_Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="1996 Stanley Cup Finals">1996</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> During the contest, the Bruins lost first-line forward <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Horton" title="Nathan Horton">Nathan Horton</a> for the remainder of the series when he suffered a serious concussion from a controversial hit by Canucks defenceman <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Rome" title="Aaron Rome">Aaron Rome</a>, who received a four-game suspension as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHL-Romesuspended_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHL-Romesuspended-114">[113]</a></sup> Returning to Vancouver for Game 5, the Canucks won 1–0 with a goal from late-season acquisition <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Lapierre" title="Maxim Lapierre">Maxim Lapierre</a> in the third period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> With an opportunity to win the Stanley Cup in Boston, Vancouver lost Game 6 by a 5–2 score. The Bruins' first four goals occurred in a span of four minutes and 14 seconds during the first period, setting a Finals record for the fastest four goals scored by a team (surpassing the previous mark of five minutes and 29 seconds set by the Montreal Canadiens in <a href="/wiki/1956_Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="1956 Stanley Cup Finals">1956</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> Hosting Game 7, the Canucks were shut-out 4–0 as Boston won their first Stanley Cup in <a href="/wiki/1972_Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="1972 Stanley Cup Finals">39 years</a>, setting off <a href="/wiki/2011_Vancouver_Stanley_Cup_riot" title="2011 Vancouver Stanley Cup riot">riots and looting</a> in downtown Vancouver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.93present">2011–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2011–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the season-opening game against the Pittsburgh Penguins on October 6, 2011, a tribute video was staged by the fans in Rogers Arena congratulating the Canucks for their record setting season and for making the Stanley Cup Finals. The team also honoured the late <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rypien" title="Rick Rypien">Rick Rypien</a> on October 18; he had been found dead at his home of a self-inflicted gunshot wound on August 15. For the rest of the season, the players wore decals on their helmets saying "37 RYP." The Canucks were also involved in a couple of trades during the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NHL_season" title="2011–12 NHL season">2011–12 season</a>, dealing <a href="/wiki/Mikael_Samuelsson" title="Mikael Samuelsson">Mikael Samuelsson</a> and the recently acquired <a href="/wiki/Marco_Sturm" title="Marco Sturm">Marco Sturm</a> to the Florida Panthers for <a href="/wiki/David_Booth_(ice_hockey)" title="David Booth (ice hockey)">David Booth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Reinprecht" title="Steven Reinprecht">Steven Reinprecht</a> and a <a href="/wiki/2013_NHL_Entry_Draft" title="2013 NHL Entry Draft">2013</a> draft pick. They would not trade again until February 27, when rookie <a href="/wiki/Cody_Hodgson" title="Cody Hodgson">Cody Hodgson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Sulzer" title="Alexander Sulzer">Alexander Sulzer</a> were traded to the Buffalo Sabres in exchange for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zach_Kassian" title="Zach Kassian">Zach Kassian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marc-Andr%C3%A9_Gragnani" title="Marc-André Gragnani">Marc-Andre Gragnani</a>. The Canucks were strong contenders for much of the 2011–12 season, catching the St. Louis Blues to secure the top seed in the Western Conference, as well as beating out the New York Rangers for their second-consecutive Presidents' Trophy. The Canucks clinched both the Western Conference and President's Trophy in their last game of the season, a 3–0 win over the Edmonton Oilers. Despite projections for another Stanley Cup run at the outset of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Stanley_Cup_playoffs" title="2012 Stanley Cup playoffs">2012 playoffs</a>, Vancouver lost their first two home games and failed to score in Game 3, as the eighth seed Los Angeles Kings took a commanding 3–0 series lead. Despite extending the series with a 3–1 win in Los Angeles, a game which saw the return of the previously-concussed Daniel Sedin, the Canucks were ultimately eliminated in five games.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vancouver_Canucks_vs_LA_Kings_at_Rogers_Arena_in_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2860" data-file-width="4290" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Vancouver_Canucks_vs_LA_Kings_at_Rogers_Arena_in_2013.jpg/300px-Vancouver_Canucks_vs_LA_Kings_at_Rogers_Arena_in_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Vancouver_Canucks_vs_LA_Kings_at_Rogers_Arena_in_2013.jpg/450px-Vancouver_Canucks_vs_LA_Kings_at_Rogers_Arena_in_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Vancouver_Canucks_vs_LA_Kings_at_Rogers_Arena_in_2013.jpg/600px-Vancouver_Canucks_vs_LA_Kings_at_Rogers_Arena_in_2013.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vancouver_Canucks_vs_LA_Kings_at_Rogers_Arena_in_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A hockey game between the Vancouver Canucks and Los Angeles Kings at Rogers Arena in March 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to the start of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_NHL_season" title="2012–13 NHL season">2012–13 season</a>, the league's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collective_bargaining_agreement" title="Collective bargaining agreement">collective bargaining agreement</a> (CBA) expired. Unable to agree on a new CBA, the NHL enacted a <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_NHL_lockout" title="2012–13 NHL lockout">lockout</a> on September 15, 2012. The lockout continued on for 119 days, which resulted in the need for a shortened season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI-over_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-SI-over-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> After the lockout ended, the Vancouver Canucks played their first game of the season on January 19, 2013, losing 7–3 to the Anaheim Ducks. Afterwards, however, they bounced back, and at one point won six games in a row before losing to the Dallas Stars at home on February 15. In the 4–3 loss, Henrik Sedin became the Canucks' all-time leading scorer, while Ryan Kesler returned to the lineup after a shoulder injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> The Canucks wore Vancouver Millionaires replica jerseys on March 16, 2013, in a game against the Detroit Red Wings to celebrate the 100-year anniversary of the Millionaires, but lost 5–2.</p>
<p>Vancouver finished the year winning their fifth consecutive Northwest Division title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> The Canucks matched up with the San Jose Sharks in the first round of the playoffs. With Cory Schneider injured, Roberto Luongo returned to the starter's role for the first two games of the series, both losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> Schneider returned for Game 3, but fared no better as the Sharks swept the Canucks in four games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014_Heritage_Classic_Anthem.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3556" data-file-width="4741" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/2014_Heritage_Classic_Anthem.jpg/300px-2014_Heritage_Classic_Anthem.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/2014_Heritage_Classic_Anthem.jpg/450px-2014_Heritage_Classic_Anthem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/2014_Heritage_Classic_Anthem.jpg/600px-2014_Heritage_Classic_Anthem.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014_Heritage_Classic_Anthem.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Vancouver Canucks and Ottawa Senators participate in the <a href="/wiki/2014_Heritage_Classic" title="2014 Heritage Classic">2014 Heritage Classic</a> at BC Place.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At an end-of-season press conference, GM Mike Gillis stated the Canucks would "hit the reset button on a number of different fronts."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> Days later, Head Coach Alain Vigneault was fired, along with assistant coaches <a href="/wiki/Rick_Bowness" title="Rick Bowness">Rick Bowness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newell_Brown" title="Newell Brown">Newell Brown</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> A month later, <a href="/wiki/John_Tortorella" title="John Tortorella">John Tortorella</a> was hired as the new head coach. Tortorella had been fired by the New York Rangers earlier in the off-season following a second round playoff loss to the Boston Bruins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Not long after Tortorella was hired, Cory Schneider was traded to the New Jersey Devils in exchange the ninth pick in the 2013 NHL Entry Draft; the Canucks chose <a href="/wiki/London_Knights" title="London Knights">London Knights</a> centre <a href="/wiki/Bo_Horvat" title="Bo Horvat">Bo Horvat</a> with the selection. The Canucks participated in their first outdoor NHL game on March 2, 2014, a match against the <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Senators" title="Ottawa Senators">Ottawa Senators</a> at <a href="/wiki/BC_Place" title="BC Place">BC Place</a>. The event was titled the <a href="/wiki/2014_Heritage_Classic" title="2014 Heritage Classic">2014 Heritage Classic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> On March 4, 2014, a day before the NHL trade deadline, Roberto Luongo was traded back to the Florida Panthers, along with Steven Anthony, in exchange for Swedish goaltender <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Markstr%C3%B6m" title="Jacob Markström">Jacob Markstrom</a> and forward <a href="/wiki/Shawn_Matthias" title="Shawn Matthias">Shawn Matthias</a>, with Luongo stating that the coach's decision not to play him at the Heritage Classic resulted in his request to be traded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> The Canucks failed to make the playoffs in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_NHL_season" title="2013–14 NHL season">2013–14 season</a>, the first time in six years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> Only one day after being eliminated from playoff contention, GM Mike Gillis was fired. Soon after, Trevor Linden was named president of hockey operations. Three weeks after Linden's hiring, John Tortorella and assistant coach Mike Sullivan were relieved of their coaching duties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Henrik_Sedin_shoots_Ryan_Miller.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2528" data-file-width="3160" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Henrik_Sedin_shoots_Ryan_Miller.JPG/220px-Henrik_Sedin_shoots_Ryan_Miller.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Henrik_Sedin_shoots_Ryan_Miller.JPG/330px-Henrik_Sedin_shoots_Ryan_Miller.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Henrik_Sedin_shoots_Ryan_Miller.JPG/440px-Henrik_Sedin_shoots_Ryan_Miller.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Henrik_Sedin_shoots_Ryan_Miller.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Henrik_Sedin" title="Henrik Sedin">Henrik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Sedin" title="Daniel Sedin">Daniel Sedin</a> seen with <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Miller" title="Ryan Miller">Ryan Miller</a> during a pre-game warm up.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On May 21, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Benning" title="Jim Benning">Jim Benning</a> was announced as general manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> On June 23, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Desjardins" title="Willie Desjardins">Willie Desjardins</a> was named the 18th head coach of the Canucks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> The team underwent a series of changes under the new management structure: veteran forward Ryan Kesler was traded to the Anaheim Ducks for <a href="/wiki/Nick_Bonino" title="Nick Bonino">Nick Bonino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luca_Sbisa" title="Luca Sbisa">Luca Sbisa</a> and first- and third-round draft selections in <a href="/wiki/2014_NHL_Entry_Draft" title="2014 NHL Entry Draft">2014</a>, and defenceman <a href="/wiki/Jason_Garrison" title="Jason Garrison">Jason Garrison</a> was traded to the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Lightning" title="Tampa Bay Lightning">Tampa Bay Lightning</a> for a second-round draft selection in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> On July 1, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Miller" title="Ryan Miller">Ryan Miller</a> signed with the Canucks, thus becoming the starting goaltender, and on July 2, <a href="/wiki/Radim_Vrbata" title="Radim Vrbata">Radim Vrbata</a> was signed to play on a line with the Sedin twins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> This season saw the team honour former General Manager and Head Coach Pat Quinn, following his recent passing, by renaming a city street after him (Pat Quinn Way) as well as having his family participate in a pregame ceremonial puck drop in a March 17, 2015 match against the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Flyers" title="Philadelphia Flyers">Philadelphia Flyers</a>. The Canucks finished second in the Pacific Division in the 2014–15 season, reaching the 100 point plateau for the ninth time in franchise history. They faced the Calgary Flames in the first round of the playoffs, losing in six games.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_information">Team information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Team information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The initial owners were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tom_Scallen" title="Tom Scallen">Tom Scallen</a>'s Medicor group. In 1972, hints of impropriety were circulating about Scallen. He was charged with stock fraud and spent the last two years of his Canuck ownership in prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> In 1974 Scallen and Medicor sold out to <a href="/wiki/Frank_Griffiths" title="Frank Griffiths">Frank Griffiths</a>. From 1988 to 1997, the Vancouver Canucks were owned by local businessman and philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Griffiths_(businessman)" title="Arthur Griffiths (businessman)">Arthur Griffiths</a>, who had inherited ownership from his father, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Griffiths" title="Frank Griffiths">Frank</a>. However, he was forced to sell his majority interest in the Canucks after overextending his resources trying to build a new arena, GM Place (currently known as <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Arena" title="Rogers Arena">Rogers Arena</a>). As a result, he sold his majority share to American billionaire <a href="/wiki/John_McCaw,_Jr." title="John McCaw, Jr.">John McCaw, Jr.</a>.</p>
<p>On November 17, 2004, the Aquilini Investment Group, headed by <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Aquilini" title="Francesco Aquilini">Francesco Aquilini</a>, purchased a 50% share in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orca_Bay_Sports_and_Entertainment" title="Orca Bay Sports and Entertainment">Orca Bay Sports and Entertainment</a> (the owners of both the Canucks franchise and Rogers Arena) from John McCaw, Jr. Prior to the sale, Aquilini and two business partners, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Gaglardi" title="Tom Gaglardi">Tom Gaglardi</a> and Ryan Beedie, had negotiated with Orca Bay for several months without concluding an agreement. In January 2005, Gaglardi and Beedie filed a lawsuit against Aquilini and Orca Bay, alleging that Aquilini and Orca Bay had acted in bad faith in concluding a deal using information obtained from their joint offer.</p>
<p>On November 8, 2006, Aquilini, along with his brothers Roberto and Paolo, purchased the remaining 50% of the Vancouver Canucks and Rogers Arena from McCaw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2007, Gaglardi and Beedie's civil lawsuit over Aquilini's purchase reached the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_British_Columbia" title="Supreme Court of British Columbia">Supreme Court of British Columbia</a>. The court ruled for Aquilini, on January 10, 2008. The court held that there was no legal partnership between Aquilini, Beedie, and Gaglardi, and that McCaw was free to sell the team to anyone he wished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 29, 2008, the company responsible for operating the Vancouver Canucks and Rogers Arena, changed its name from Orca Bay Sports and Entertainment to <a href="/wiki/Canucks_Sports_%26_Entertainment" title="Canucks Sports &amp; Entertainment">Canucks Sports &amp; Entertainment</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_arenas">Home arenas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Home arenas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pacificcoliseum.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Pacificcoliseum.jpg/200px-Pacificcoliseum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Pacificcoliseum.jpg/300px-Pacificcoliseum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Pacificcoliseum.jpg/400px-Pacificcoliseum.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Pacific Coliseum, home of the Canucks from 1970–1995.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rogers_Arena.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Rogers_Arena.jpg/200px-Rogers_Arena.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Rogers_Arena.jpg/300px-Rogers_Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Rogers_Arena.jpg/400px-Rogers_Arena.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Rogers Arena, current home of the Canucks.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Canucks play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Arena" title="Rogers Arena">Rogers Arena</a>. The stadium opened in 1995 as General Motors Place, and seats up to 18,890 for Canucks games. Rogers Arena was also the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>' ice hockey venue. The arena is owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/Canucks_Sports_%26_Entertainment" title="Canucks Sports &amp; Entertainment">Canucks Sports &amp; Entertainment</a>. Before moving to Rogers Arena, the Canucks played their home games at <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coliseum" title="Pacific Coliseum">Pacific Coliseum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hastings_Park" title="Hastings Park">Hastings Park</a> for 25 years. The arena currently holds 16,281 for ice hockey, though capacity at its opening was 15,713. During the 2010 Olympics, it was the venue for <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating" title="Figure skating">figure skating</a> and <a href="/wiki/Short_track_speed_skating" title="Short track speed skating">short track speed skating</a>. The Pacific Coliseum was also the home of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hockey_League" title="Western Hockey League">Western Hockey League</a> (WHL)'s <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Giants" title="Vancouver Giants">Vancouver Giants</a> from 2001 to 2016.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logos_and_jerseys">Logos and jerseys</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Logos and jerseys">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The team has gone through thirteen different logo and jersey changes in its history.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VancouverCanucks1970s.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="252" data-file-width="371" height="82" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bf/VancouverCanucks1970s.svg/120px-VancouverCanucks1970s.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bf/VancouverCanucks1970s.svg/180px-VancouverCanucks1970s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bf/VancouverCanucks1970s.svg/240px-VancouverCanucks1970s.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VancouverCanucks1970s.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "Stick-in-Rink", 1970–1978; alternate logo, 2003–2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The team's first NHL jerseys, worn from the inaugural season of 1970–71 (modified for the 1972–73 season) until the end of the 1977–78 season, featured a hockey stick in the shape of a shallow "V" superimposed on a blue rink-shaped rectangle forming the letter "C", designed by North Vancouver artist Joe Borovich. A modified version of this logo is still in use, as a shoulder patch on the team's current jerseys and as the primary logo of their alternate jerseys.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1977%E2%80%9378_NHL_season" title="1977–78 NHL season">1978</a>, aiming for a more aggressive image, the organization asked San Francisco-based design agency Beyl &amp; Boyd to design new uniforms. These consisted of a huge yellow, red-orange and black striped "V" coming down from the shoulders (suggesting "victory", according to its designers). Hockey writer Stephen Cole described it as looking like "a punch in the eye".</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canucks_Logo_1978_to_1997.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="121" data-file-width="181" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b5/Canucks_Logo_1978_to_1997.svg/120px-Canucks_Logo_1978_to_1997.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b5/Canucks_Logo_1978_to_1997.svg/180px-Canucks_Logo_1978_to_1997.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b5/Canucks_Logo_1978_to_1997.svg/240px-Canucks_Logo_1978_to_1997.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canucks_Logo_1978_to_1997.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "Flying Skate", 1978–1997.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The "Flying V" theme was abandoned in <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_NHL_season" title="1985–86 NHL season">1985</a>, to feature the team's emblem on the front rather than the "V" (the emblem had previously been worn only on the arms). The logo consisted of the word "Canucks" in a diagonal slant as part the blade of a skate and was designed by San Francisco graphic artist Mike Bull. The logo, with its laser-like design, was sometimes referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a>" logo, the "waffle iron", the "plate of spaghetti", and most commonly as the "Flying Skate."</p>
<p>The yellow home jerseys were scrapped in 1989 in favour of more conventional white ones, and the triangular shoulder stripes which adorned the post-"V" jerseys were discarded as well. The new incarnation was worn from 1989–92, when a subtle change was made – and went largely unnoticed for the rest of the jersey's lifespan. The orange was changed to red, and the deep "gold" colour was changed to a much brighter yellow, reportedly because jersey-maker <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CCM_(The_Hockey_Company)" title="CCM (The Hockey Company)">CCM</a> no longer produced the required hues. In 1996, an alternate jersey was introduced, retaining the "Flying Skate" logo, but using a salmon colour graduating to black near the bottom.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vancouver_Canucks_logo_(1998%E2%80%932007).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="482" data-file-width="500" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Vancouver_Canucks_logo_%281998%E2%80%932007%29.svg/120px-Vancouver_Canucks_logo_%281998%E2%80%932007%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Vancouver_Canucks_logo_%281998%E2%80%932007%29.svg/180px-Vancouver_Canucks_logo_%281998%E2%80%932007%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Vancouver_Canucks_logo_%281998%E2%80%932007%29.svg/240px-Vancouver_Canucks_logo_%281998%E2%80%932007%29.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vancouver_Canucks_logo_(1998%E2%80%932007).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Orca logo, 1997–2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_NHL_season" title="1997–98 NHL season">1997</a> the Canucks unveiled a new logo, in which a <a href="/wiki/Haida_people" title="Haida people">Haida</a>-style orca breaking out of a patch of ice forms a stylized "C." The logo has been much-maligned, accused of being a blatant reference to their parent company, Orca Bay (now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canucks_Sports_and_Entertainment" title="Canucks Sports and Entertainment">Canucks Sports and Entertainment</a>). At the time, General Manager <a href="/wiki/Pat_Quinn_(ice_hockey)" title="Pat Quinn (ice hockey)">Pat Quinn</a> discussed wanting to have a West Coast colour scheme, and overall West Coast themes in the logo; the colour scheme included blue, red and silver. Beginning in 2001, an alternate jersey was utilized, with contrasting shoulder patches and a blue-to-maroon graduated colour in the body. In <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NHL_season" title="2006–07 NHL season">2006</a>, these gradient-coloured alternate jerseys were officially replaced with the popular, royal blue "Stick-in-Rink" uniforms from the 1970s.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;max-width:372px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vancouver_Canucks_Home_Logo.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="482" data-file-width="500" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Vancouver_Canucks_Home_Logo.svg/120px-Vancouver_Canucks_Home_Logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Vancouver_Canucks_Home_Logo.svg/180px-Vancouver_Canucks_Home_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Vancouver_Canucks_Home_Logo.svg/240px-Vancouver_Canucks_Home_Logo.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Canucks Home Logo; 2007–present.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:246px;max-width:246px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canucks_Wordmark.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="167" data-file-width="350" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Canucks_Wordmark.jpg/244px-Canucks_Wordmark.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d8/Canucks_Wordmark.jpg 1.5x" width="244"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Canucks Wordmark Logo.; 2007–present.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Little more than halfway through the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NHL_season" title="2006–07 NHL season">2006–07 season</a>, the Canucks announced that they would be changing their jerseys once again. The new jersey was unveiled prior to training camp, on August 29, 2007. It featured the same orca design present on their previous jerseys, but the colour scheme was changed to their "retro" colours of royal blue and kelly green. Additionally, the word "Vancouver" was added to the chest area above the orca. This move was seen as a way to connect the NHL Canucks' uniform to that of the WHL team, whose members wore uniforms with the word "Canucks" along the top in a similar arched design.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The actual jerseys themselves were changed to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rbk_Edge" title="Rbk Edge">Rbk Edge</a> design, along with all other teams in the NHL. The introduction was largely greeted with disappointment from fans and sports commentators, who criticized the uniforms for looking like a "copy and paste" of those from the past.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <i>The Vancouver Sun</i> described the new look as "decidedly unpopular."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:306px;max-width:306px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:180px;max-width:180px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VancouverCanucksStickNew.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="257" data-file-width="350" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/VancouverCanucksStickNew.png/178px-VancouverCanucksStickNew.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/VancouverCanucksStickNew.png/267px-VancouverCanucksStickNew.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/0f/VancouverCanucksStickNew.png 2x" width="178"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">"The Stick-in-Rink", modified; alternate logo, 2007–present.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johnnycanucklogo.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="132" data-file-width="121" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e2/Johnnycanucklogo.svg/120px-Johnnycanucklogo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e2/Johnnycanucklogo.svg/180px-Johnnycanucklogo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e2/Johnnycanucklogo.svg/240px-Johnnycanucklogo.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">"<a href="/wiki/Johnny_Canuck" title="Johnny Canuck">Johnny Canuck</a>" Reebok third jersey shoulder logo, modified; 2008–present.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On November 14, 2008, prior to their Sport Celebrities Festival, the Canucks released their new RBK Edge Third Jersey. While staying with the colours of Vancouver, and combining the old with the new, the jersey looks very similar to their home jersey. The modernized "Stick-in-Rink" logo unveiled the previous year on the shoulder of the main jerseys is used as the main crest. On the shoulder, a "V" with the head of <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Canuck" title="Johnny Canuck">Johnny Canuck</a> on top is used. This is the first time in team history since joining the NHL that Johnny Canuck has appeared on a Vancouver uniform. <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> rated it 13th overall out of the 19 third jerseys released for the 2008 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>On opening night October 9, 2010, the Canucks revealed jerseys they would wear for select games during their 40th Anniversary season. They look exactly like the jerseys the team wore in their early years, only with the addition of <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> manufacturing the jerseys. The jerseys sport a 40th Anniversary patch on the upper-right chest commemorating their 40th season. Just like the early years, they also bear no player names, only numbers, with permission from the NHL.</p>
<p>On August 13, 2015, the Canucks announced that they would be wearing their 1990s Flying Skate jerseys for a February 13, 2016 game against the Toronto Maple Leafs to honour the 20th Anniversary of Rogers Arena. They attempted to do this in the previous season to honour Pat Quinn, but were unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Vancouver_Canucks_broadcasters" title="List of Vancouver Canucks broadcasters">List of Vancouver Canucks broadcasters</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1272" data-file-width="1353" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg/275px-Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg/413px-Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg/550px-Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg.png 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Vancouver Canucks broadcast area in red.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After a relationship with <a href="/wiki/CKNW" title="CKNW">CKNW</a> stretching since the Canucks joined the NHL in 1970, the Canucks entered into a new radio broadcast deal in 2006 with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CKST_(AM)" title="CKST (AM)">TSN Radio 1040</a> (previously known as Team 1040) – an <a href="/wiki/AM_broadcasting" title="AM broadcasting">AM</a> sports/talk station. <a href="/wiki/John_Shorthouse" title="John Shorthouse">John Shorthouse</a> continues to call the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Play-by-play" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a>, as he has since 1999, though with his role on the Canucks' television broadcasts becoming more prominent in recent years, he is replaced for approximately 50 games per season by Jon Abbott. He is joined with colour commentary by <a href="/wiki/Dave_Tomlinson" title="Dave Tomlinson">Dave Tomlinson</a>, who has been with the broadcasts since 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> The games aired on 14 stations across <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canucks_Mascot_Fin_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2525" data-file-width="3366" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Canucks_Mascot_Fin_2009.jpg/250px-Canucks_Mascot_Fin_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Canucks_Mascot_Fin_2009.jpg/375px-Canucks_Mascot_Fin_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Canucks_Mascot_Fin_2009.jpg/500px-Canucks_Mascot_Fin_2009.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canucks_Mascot_Fin_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fin, the official mascot of the Vancouver Canucks, in 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to national TV broadcasts on <i><a href="/wiki/Hockey_Night_in_Canada" title="Hockey Night in Canada">Hockey Night in Canada</a></i>, the Canucks also have arrangements with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rogers_Sportsnet" title="Rogers Sportsnet">Sportsnet Pacific</a>. These games are called by Shorthouse and former Canucks goaltender <a href="/wiki/John_Garrett_(ice_hockey)" title="John Garrett (ice hockey)">John Garrett</a>. Since the 2010–11 season, Sportsnet Vancouver Hockey, a companion channel to the new national sports channel <a href="/wiki/Sportsnet_One" title="Sportsnet One">Sportsnet One</a>, has aired Canucks regional telecasts that are not able to fit into Sportsnet Pacific's schedule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> The regional games are only available for viewers living in <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yukon_Territory" title="Yukon Territory">Yukon</a>.</p>
<p>Additionally, as of the 2010–11 season, Rogers acquired the <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">naming rights</a> to the Canucks' home arena.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Vancouver Canucks' <a href="/wiki/Mascot" title="Mascot">mascot</a> is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anthropomorphic" title="Anthropomorphic">anthropomorphic</a> <a href="/wiki/Killer_whale" title="Killer whale">killer whale</a> (orca) named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fin_the_Whale" title="Fin the Whale">Fin the Whale</a>. He is often seen banging a <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a> drum, or skating around during intermissions firing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-shirts" title="T-shirts">t-shirts</a> out of a compressed air cannon. On occasion, "smoke" also comes out of the blowhole on his head. Fin is known for his "chomping" where he bites the heads of fans.</p>
<p>Two fans of the Canucks became unofficial mascots of their team at the end of 2009, donning <a href="/wiki/Zentai" title="Zentai">zentai</a>-style, skin-tight green bodysuits in slightly different shades of green as <a href="/wiki/The_Green_Men" title="The Green Men">The Green Men</a>, and have been known to accompany their team on road games, as they did in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="2011 Stanley Cup Finals">2011 Stanley Cup Finals</a> to the <a href="/wiki/TD_Garden" title="TD Garden">TD Garden</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a>. In November 2014, the Green Men announced that <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Vancouver_Canucks_season" title="2014–15 Vancouver Canucks season">2014–15</a> was to be their final season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup></p>

<dl>
<dt><b>Notes:</b></dt>
</dl>
<p><i>Bure wore number 10 for five of his seven seasons in Vancouver. He wore number 96 during the 1995–96 and 1996–97 seasons before returning to number 10 during the 1997–98 season.</i></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Numbers_taken_out_of_circulation">Numbers taken out of circulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Numbers taken out of circulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Although not officially retired, the following numbers are no longer issued by the Canucks:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>11</b> – <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Maki" title="Wayne Maki">Wayne Maki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winger_(ice_hockey)" title="Winger (ice hockey)">LW</a>, 1970–1973, taken out of circulation following his death from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain_cancer" title="Brain cancer">brain cancer</a> on May 1, 1974. <a href="/wiki/Mark_Messier" title="Mark Messier">Mark Messier</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Center_(ice_hockey)" title="Center (ice hockey)">C</a>, 1997–2000) is the only Canucks player to have worn it since.</li>
<li><b>28</b> – <a href="/wiki/Luc_Bourdon" title="Luc Bourdon">Luc Bourdon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Defenceman" title="Defenceman">D</a>, 2006–2008, taken out of circulation following his death in a motorcycle accident on May 29, 2008. Wore No. 4 in 2006–07.</li>
<li><b>37</b> – <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rypien" title="Rick Rypien">Rick Rypien</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Center_(ice_hockey)" title="Center (ice hockey)">C</a>, 2005–2010, taken out of circulation following his death from suicide on August 15, 2011. Wore No. 15 from 2005 to 2007.</li>
<li><b>38</b> – <a href="/wiki/Pavol_Demitra" title="Pavol Demitra">Pavol Demitra</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Center_(ice_hockey)" title="Center (ice hockey)">C</a>, 2008–2010, taken out of circulation following his death with <a href="/wiki/Lokomotiv_Yaroslavl" title="Lokomotiv Yaroslavl">Kontinental Hockey League team Lokomotiv Yaroslavl</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Lokomotiv_Yaroslavl_air_disaster" title="2011 Lokomotiv Yaroslavl air disaster">Lokomotiv Air Disaster</a> on September 7, 2011. <a href="/wiki/Victor_Oreskovich" title="Victor Oreskovich">Victor Oreskovich</a> wore it in <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Vancouver_Canucks_season" title="2010–11 Vancouver Canucks season">2011</a> following Demitra's departure, but before his death.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ring_of_Honour_inductees"><a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Canucks_Ring_of_Honour" title="Vancouver Canucks Ring of Honour">Ring of Honour inductees</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ring of Honour inductees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orland_Kurtenbach" title="Orland Kurtenbach">Orland Kurtenbach</a>, C, 1970–1974, inducted October 26, 2010.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kirk_McLean" title="Kirk McLean">Kirk McLean</a>, G, 1987–1998, inducted November 24, 2010.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Gradin" title="Thomas Gradin">Thomas Gradin</a>, C, 1978–1986, inducted January 24, 2011.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harold_Snepsts" title="Harold Snepsts">Harold Snepsts</a>, D, 1974–1984; 1988–1990, inducted March 14, 2011.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pat_Quinn_(ice_hockey)" title="Pat Quinn (ice hockey)">Pat Quinn</a>, D, 1970–1972; President &amp; General manager, 1987–1997; Head Coach, 1991–1995, inducted April 13, 2014.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mattias_%C3%96hlund" title="Mattias Öhlund">Mattias Öhlund</a>, D, 1997–2009, inducted December 16, 2016.</li>
</ul>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2012_NHL_Entry_Draft" title="2012 NHL Entry Draft">2012 NHL Entry Draft</a>, draftees were given jerseys with an <a href="/wiki/Apostrophe" title="Apostrophe">apostrophe</a> before the 12 (i.e. <b>’12</b>), to distinguish them from the 12 that was retired in honor of Smyl. (NHL draft custom states that draftees are given jerseys with the number indicating the year they were drafted.)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Needs source (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_captains">Team captains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Team captains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linden3cropped1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="645" height="349" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Linden3cropped1.JPG/250px-Linden3cropped1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Linden3cropped1.JPG/375px-Linden3cropped1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Linden3cropped1.JPG/500px-Linden3cropped1.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linden3cropped1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Trevor Linden, who was drafted by the Canucks, served as team captain from 1991–97. He is currently the team's President of Hockey Operations and Alternate Governor.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There have been 13 Canucks players who have served as the captain. The franchise's first captain was <a href="/wiki/Orland_Kurtenbach" title="Orland Kurtenbach">Orland Kurtenbach</a>, who captained the team until his retirement in 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> The longest-tenured Canucks captain was <a href="/wiki/Stan_Smyl" title="Stan Smyl">Stan Smyl</a>, who was appointed for eight seasons. <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Linden" title="Trevor Linden">Trevor Linden</a>, who captained from 1990 to 1997, played 16 seasons with the Canucks, a franchise high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> Swedish winger <a href="/wiki/Markus_N%C3%A4slund" title="Markus Näslund">Markus Naslund</a>, who captained for seven seasons<sup class="reference" id="ref_Note1a"><a href="#endnote_Note1a">[a]</a></sup>, was the only non-Canadian to have captained the Canucks until fellow Swede <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Sedin" title="Henrik Sedin">Henrik Sedin</a> was named captain for the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NHL_season" title="2010–11 NHL season">2010–11 season</a>. Smyl and Sedin are the only Canucks captains to have spent their entire NHL playing careers with the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>Though <a href="/wiki/Goaltender" title="Goaltender">goaltenders</a> are not permitted to act as captains during games, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Luongo" title="Roberto Luongo">Roberto Luongo</a> served as the captain from 2008 to 2010, but because of the NHL rule against goaltender captains, the league did not allow Luongo to serve as on-ice captain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-official_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-official-154">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Luongo_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Luongo-155">[154]</a></sup> In his place, the three alternate captains were responsible for dealing with <a href="/wiki/Official_(ice_hockey)" title="Official (ice hockey)">officials</a> during games. They also handled ceremonial <a href="/wiki/Face-off" title="Face-off">face-offs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Luongo_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-Luongo-155">[154]</a></sup> Luongo was not permitted to wear the "C" on his jersey. Instead, he incorporated it into the artwork on the front of one of his <a href="/wiki/Goaltender_mask" title="Goaltender mask">masks</a>, which he occasionally wore for the early months of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Vancouver_Canucks_season" title="2008–09 Vancouver Canucks season">2008–09 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Orland_Kurtenbach" title="Orland Kurtenbach">Orland Kurtenbach</a>, 1970–1974</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Boudrias" title="André Boudrias">Andre Boudrias</a>, 1975–1976</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chris_Oddleifson" title="Chris Oddleifson">Chris Oddleifson</a>, 1976–1977</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Don_Lever" title="Don Lever">Don Lever</a>, 1977–1979</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kevin_McCarthy_(ice_hockey)" title="Kevin McCarthy (ice hockey)">Kevin McCarthy</a>, 1979–1982</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stan_Smyl" title="Stan Smyl">Stan Smyl</a>, 1982–1990</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dan_Quinn_(ice_hockey)" title="Dan Quinn (ice hockey)">Dan Quinn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doug_Lidster" title="Doug Lidster">Doug Lidster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Linden" title="Trevor Linden">Trevor Linden</a>, 1990–1991 <small>(tri-captains)</small></li>
<li>Trevor Linden, 1991–1997</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Messier" title="Mark Messier">Mark Messier</a>, 1997–2000</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Markus_N%C3%A4slund" title="Markus Näslund">Markus Naslund</a>, 2000–2008</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roberto_Luongo" title="Roberto Luongo">Roberto Luongo</a>, 2008–2010</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Henrik_Sedin" title="Henrik Sedin">Henrik Sedin</a>, 2010–<i>present</i></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Draft_picks">Draft picks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Draft picks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Vancouver_Canucks_draft_picks" title="List of Vancouver Canucks draft picks">List of Vancouver Canucks draft picks</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Henrik_Sedin_02-2015a.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3143" data-file-width="2244" height="350" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Henrik_Sedin_02-2015a.JPG/250px-Henrik_Sedin_02-2015a.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Henrik_Sedin_02-2015a.JPG/375px-Henrik_Sedin_02-2015a.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Henrik_Sedin_02-2015a.JPG/500px-Henrik_Sedin_02-2015a.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Henrik_Sedin_02-2015a.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Canucks selected Henrik Sedin third overall in the 1999 NHL Entry Draft. He has served as the team's captain since 2010.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Canucks selected <a href="/wiki/Dale_Tallon" title="Dale Tallon">Dale Tallon</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Defenceman" title="Defenceman">defenceman</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Marlboros" title="Toronto Marlboros">Toronto Marlboros</a> with their first pick, second overall in the <a href="/wiki/1970_NHL_Amateur_Draft" title="1970 NHL Amateur Draft">1970 NHL Amateur Draft</a>. In 1978, they drafted <a href="/wiki/Stan_Smyl" title="Stan Smyl">Stan Smyl</a> from the <a href="/wiki/New_Westminster_Bruins" title="New Westminster Bruins">New Westminster Bruins</a>. Ten years later, the Canucks also drafted <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Linden" title="Trevor Linden">Trevor Linden</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Medicine_Hat_Tigers" title="Medicine Hat Tigers">Medicine Hat Tigers</a> in <a href="/wiki/1988_NHL_Entry_Draft" title="1988 NHL Entry Draft">1988</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> The Canucks have had 13 top-five draft picks in franchise history, but have never had the first overall pick. The Canucks are one of the two franchises in the NHL to have drafted two twin brothers in the same year. They drafted <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Sedin" title="Daniel Sedin">Daniel Sedin</a> second overall and <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Sedin" title="Henrik Sedin">Henrik Sedin</a> third overall in <a href="/wiki/1999_NHL_Entry_Draft" title="1999 NHL Entry Draft">1999</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Two players from British Columbia have been selected by the Canucks in the first round of an NHL Entry Draft: <a href="/wiki/Cam_Neely" title="Cam Neely">Cam Neely</a> in <a href="/wiki/1983_NHL_Entry_Draft" title="1983 NHL Entry Draft">1983</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jake_Virtanen" title="Jake Virtanen">Jake Virtanen</a>, taken 6th overall in <a href="/wiki/2014_NHL_Entry_Draft" title="2014 NHL Entry Draft">2014</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_scoring_leaders">Franchise scoring leaders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Franchise scoring leaders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_coaches">Head coaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Head coaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Vancouver_Canucks_head_coaches" title="List of Vancouver Canucks head coaches">List of Vancouver Canucks head coaches</a></div>
<p>There have been 18 <a href="/wiki/Head_coach" title="Head coach">head coaches</a> for the Canucks. The franchise's first head coach was <a href="/wiki/Hal_Laycoe" title="Hal Laycoe">Hal Laycoe</a>, who coached the Canucks for two seasons. <a href="/wiki/Alain_Vigneault" title="Alain Vigneault">Alain Vigneault</a> coached the most games of any Canucks head coach with 540 games, and has the most points all-time with the Canucks, with 683. He is followed by <a href="/wiki/Marc_Crawford" title="Marc Crawford">Marc Crawford</a>, who has 586 points all-time with the Canucks. Vigneault also has the most points in a season of any Canucks coach, with 117 in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NHL_season" title="2010–11 NHL season">2010–11 season</a>. <a href="/wiki/Roger_Neilson" title="Roger Neilson">Roger Neilson</a> is the only <a href="/wiki/Hockey_Hall_of_Fame" title="Hockey Hall of Fame">Hockey Hall of Fame</a> inductee to coach the Canucks. Quinn and Vigneault are the only two Canucks head coaches to win a <a href="/wiki/Jack_Adams_Award" title="Jack Adams Award">Jack Adams Award</a> with the team. <a href="/wiki/Bill_LaForge" title="Bill LaForge">Bill LaForge</a>, who coached the start of the 1984 season, has the least points with the Canucks, with 10. <a href="/wiki/Harry_Neale" title="Harry Neale">Harry Neale</a> served the most terms as head coach of the Canucks with three while Pat Quinn served two. Vigneault was the head coach of the Canucks from the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NHL_season" title="2006–07 NHL season">2006–07 season</a> through to the end of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_NHL_season" title="2012–13 NHL season">2012–13 season</a>. Vigneault was fired on May 22, 2013, after first round playoff exits in the previous two seasons, and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/John_Tortorella" title="John Tortorella">John Tortorella</a> on June 25, 2013. Tortorella was fired at the end of the following season, on May 1, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> On June 23, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Desjardins" title="Willie Desjardins">Willie Desjardins</a> was named the team's 18th head coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_trophies">Awards and trophies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Awards and trophies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Vancouver_Canucks_award_winners" title="List of Vancouver Canucks award winners">List of Vancouver Canucks award winners</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NHL">NHL</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: NHL">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div style="float:left; width:48%;">
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Clarence_S._Campbell_Bowl" title="Clarence S. Campbell Bowl">Clarence S. Campbell Bowl</a></b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_NHL_season" title="1981–82 NHL season">1981–82</a>, <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_NHL_season" title="1993–94 NHL season">1993–94</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NHL_season" title="2010–11 NHL season">2010–11</a></li>
</ul>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Presidents%27_Trophy" title="Presidents' Trophy">Presidents' Trophy</a></b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NHL_season" title="2010–11 NHL season">2010–11</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NHL_season" title="2011–12 NHL season">2011–12</a></li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise">Franchise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Franchise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyclone_Taylor_Award" title="Cyclone Taylor Award">Cyclone Taylor Award</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_H._McLean_Trophy" title="Cyrus H. McLean Trophy">Cyrus H. McLean Trophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babe_Pratt_Trophy" title="Babe Pratt Trophy">Babe Pratt Trophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molson_Cup" title="Molson Cup">Molson Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fred_J._Hume_Award" title="Fred J. Hume Award">Fred J. Hume Award</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Bure_Most_Exciting_Player_Award" title="Pavel Bure Most Exciting Player Award">Pavel Bure Most Exciting Player Award</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_individual_records">Franchise individual records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Franchise individual records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Vancouver_Canucks_records" title="List of Vancouver Canucks records">List of Vancouver Canucks records</a></div>
<ul>
<li>Most goals in a season: <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Bure" title="Pavel Bure">Pavel Bure</a>, 60 (<a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_NHL_season" title="1992–93 NHL season">1992–93</a> and <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_NHL_season" title="1993–94 NHL season">1993–94</a>)</li>
<li>Most assists in a season: <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Sedin" title="Henrik Sedin">Henrik Sedin</a>, 83 (<a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NHL_season" title="2009–10 NHL season">2009–10</a>)</li>
<li>Most points in a season: <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Sedin" title="Henrik Sedin">Henrik Sedin</a>, 112 (<a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NHL_season" title="2009–10 NHL season">2009–10</a>)</li>
<li>Highest plus/minus in a season: <a href="/wiki/Christian_Ehrhoff" title="Christian Ehrhoff">Christian Ehrhoff</a>, 36 (<a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NHL_season" title="2009–10 NHL season">2009–10</a>); <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Sedin" title="Daniel Sedin">Daniel Sedin</a>, 36 (<a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NHL_season" title="2009–10 NHL season">2009–10</a>), tied</li>
<li>Most penalty minutes in a season: <a href="/wiki/Donald_Brashear" title="Donald Brashear">Donald Brashear</a>, 372 (<a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_NHL_season" title="1997–98 NHL season">1997–98</a>)</li>
<li>Most points in a season, defenceman: <a href="/wiki/Doug_Lidster" title="Doug Lidster">Doug Lidster</a>, 63 (<a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_NHL_season" title="1986–87 NHL season">1986–87</a>)</li>
<li>Most points in a season, rookie: <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Hlinka" title="Ivan Hlinka">Ivan Hlinka</a>, 60 (<a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_NHL_season" title="1981–82 NHL season">1981–82</a>); Pavel Bure, 60 (<a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_NHL_season" title="1991–92 NHL season">1991–92</a>), tied</li>
<li>Most wins in a season: <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Luongo" title="Roberto Luongo">Roberto Luongo</a>, 47 (<a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NHL_season" title="2006–07 NHL season">2006–07</a>)</li>
<li>Most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shutouts#Ice_hockey" title="Shutouts">shutouts</a> in a season: <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Luongo" title="Roberto Luongo">Roberto Luongo</a>, 9 (<a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_NHL_season" title="2008–09 NHL season">2008–09</a>)</li>
<li>Lowest <a href="/wiki/Goals_against_average" title="Goals against average">GAA</a> in a season (min. 30 <a href="/wiki/Games_played" title="Games played">GP</a>): <a href="/wiki/Cory_Schneider" title="Cory Schneider">Cory Schneider</a>, 1.96 (<a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NHL_season" title="2011–12 NHL season">2011–12</a>)</li>
<li>Best <a href="/wiki/Save_percentage" title="Save percentage">SV%</a> in a season (min. 30 GP): <a href="/wiki/Cory_Schneider" title="Cory Schneider">Cory Schneider</a>, .937 (<a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NHL_season" title="2011–12 NHL season">2011–12</a>)</li>
<li>Fastest goal recorded by a Canuck: <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Burrows" title="Alexandre Burrows">Alexandre Burrows</a>, 6 seconds (<a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_NHL_season" title="2012–13 NHL season">2012–13</a>)</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vancouver_Canucks&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-78">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example: decreased tolerance for impeding a player as he is skating, four-foot increase length-wise in the offensive zones, abolishment of the two-line pass rule (i.e. passing the puck from the defending zone to the opposing side of centre) and a decrease in goaltending equipment size.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
